    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer4280604499173744862">Sous son écharpe élimée et ses lunettes de myope, Ophélie cache des dons singuliers : elle peut lire le passé des objets et traverser les miroirs.   <span id="freeText4280604499173744862" style="display:none">Sous son écharpe élimée et ses lunettes de myope, Ophélie cache des dons singuliers : elle peut lire le passé des objets et traverser les miroirs. Elle vit paisiblement sur l'Arche d'Anima quand on la fiance à Thorn, du puissant clan des Dragons. La jeune fille doit quitter sa famille et le suivre à la Citacielle, capitale flottante du Pôle. À quelle fin a-t-elle été choisie ? Pourquoi doit-elle dissimuler sa véritable identité ? Sans le savoir, Ophélie devient le jouet d'un complot mortel.<br /><br />Une héroïne inoubliable, un univers riche et foisonnant, une intrigue implacable. Découvrez le premier livre d'une grande saga fantastique et le talent d'un nouvel auteur à l'imaginaire saisissant.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is a little bit, it is more insinuated than anything. The main character is in an arranged marriage and you can see the male lead start to devel<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is a little bit, it is more insinuated than anything. The main character is in an arranged marriage and you can see the male lead start to develop an interested/feeling for the heroine, but this mainly happens towards then end of the book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2483392848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483392848" />
    <a title="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox"><img alt="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546189365p2/58160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483392848?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox">Emily (Books with Emily Fox)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483392848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1062002404332336881">(2.5?) That was... something. <br/><br/>I have very conflicted thoughts about this book. The world building was interesting and so was the magic system but I had lots of issues with the book. For a matriarchal society seems pretty backward.<br/><br/><br/>Girl who's not like other ones because... she has glasses!! She is send to a different part of the world where she will have to marry someone she doesn't want to.<br/><br/>Interesting world and magic system but not explained enough. It could be due to us seeing it all through the</span>
  <span id="freeText1062002404332336881" style="display:none">(2.5?) That was... something. <br /><br />I have very conflicted thoughts about this book. The world building was interesting and so was the magic system but I had lots of issues with the book. For a matriarchal society seems pretty backward.<br /><br /><br />Girl who's not like other ones because... she has glasses!! She is send to a different part of the world where she will have to marry someone she doesn't want to.<br /><br />Interesting world and magic system but not explained enough. It could be due to us seeing it all through the eyes of a character who knows nothing so I hope to see more.<br /><br />The writing was strange. Not just because it was in French.<br /><br />Slow paced. Pretty Character driven and a lot in the head of the main character since she spends a lot of time not talking. Main character is so bland, it was hard to root for her. It’s nice to not have the same strong warrior for once but man is she bland.<br />Idk if it was meant for the reader to see themselves in her. Average with glasses. Oh so clumsy. <br />But I was having flashbacks from Twilight.<br /><br />Things eventually picked up and became more interesting but the romance was... what?<br /><br />“I got used to you” and she instantly thinks he’s madly in love with her. Girl sit down.<br /><br />I think I’ll continue. Not sure when.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1062002404332336881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1695316482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1695316482" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695316482?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=what-a-jerk">what-a-jerk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=cringeworthy">cringeworthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=french-literature">french-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=annoying-mc">annoying-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=you-ve-got-to-be-kidding-me">you-ve-got-to-be-kidding-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695316482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9537929942006824291"><b><u>EDIT</u> : a quick foreword because I'm t i r e d, and look at me! I'm writing in bold font, what a monster *shivers*<br/><br/>1) <u>I've never attacked the author.</u> My review is solely focused on the book and the book only. Goodreads offers me the opportunity, as a reader, to give my honest opinion. I... took it. It's that simple. <br/> <br/>2) <u>The use of profanity is a stylistic choice.</u> Sometimes I curse, others I don't and (surprise surprise) I'm actually able to interact in a different way. After finishing this novel t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9537929942006824291" style="display:none"><b><u>EDIT</u> : a quick foreword because I'm t i r e d, and look at me! I'm writing in bold font, what a monster *shivers*<br><br>1) <u>I've never attacked the author.</u> My review is solely focused on the book and the book only. Goodreads offers me the opportunity, as a reader, to give my honest opinion. I... took it. It's that simple. <br> <br>2) <u>The use of profanity is a stylistic choice.</u> Sometimes I curse, others I don't and (surprise surprise) I'm actually able to interact in a different way. After finishing this novel though, I made the choice that appeared the most suitable to ME, to express MY opinion, and yes, it absolutely involved a savvy blend of English and French curse words. Like it, don't like it, at this point I really don't care. <br><br>3) As a French citizen, I find stereotypes about French people rather annoying <u>so maybe let's not, I don't know, jump at the chance to prove them right?</u> I mean, congrats! I have never gotten more insulting comments and threatening private messages than on this/because of this review. It's like you <i>want</i> people to think that French don't know how to deal with criticism, honestly? <br><br>4) You have a review space. <u>USE IT.</u> Oh, and no, "you read it wrong" does not in fact equal constructive criticism. It doesn't prove anything, except that for some reason you can't let it <i>go.</i> It's been two years. Give it a break maybe? <br><br>Now if you'd please stop acting like my review is "harming" a <i>tremendously popular novel,</i> it'd be great. Have a good day. <br><br><u>MY REVIEW</u></b> <br><br>► <b>Note</b> : This review will be divided into two parts : the first one in English <i>et la deuxième en français.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468375992i/19698033._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let me start by saying that my two parts won't be sole translations : first because translating bores me to death, and secondly because given the fact that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18043539.Les_Fianc_s_de_l_hiver" title="Les Fiancés de l'hiver by Christelle Dabos" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Fiancés de l'hiver</a> is a French book, I just don't see the point in rambling in English about it. <br><br>Yet.<br><br>I still needed to express my opinion this way because I believe that this book demonstrated something that we find in a fair amount of YA novels : <b>a complete contradiction between what we're told and what we <i>really</i> get.</b> <br><br>What we're told is that the society pictured is <b>matriarchal and somehow empowering for women.</b> <br><b>What we get is a misogynist piece of shit</b>. No, really. I am not exaggerating. <br><br>1) <b>The heroine's opinion is constantly overlooked, even when she expresses clearly her disapproval, which is rare enough already</b>. The members of her family repeatedly state how she must : <br>a) obey her fiancé whatever it takes ; <br>b) change in order to please him ; <br>c) never ever go against his orders. <br><br>2) <b>Every woman apart from the heroine or her aunt is pictured like a manipulative bitch</b>. Every. Fucking. One. Almost all the women we meet are vapid, superficial, and often straight on mean. <br><br>3) <b>To add insult to injury, sex is portrayed as being fundamentally impure, especially, of course, when women are involved</b>. <u>All cheaters are women</u>, and the whole thing stinks of double-standards. The men's actions are overlooked when the women are called bitches. I mean, for fuck sake. <br><br>4) <b>There is this fucking piece of shit of character, Archibald</b>. God, that guy. He manages to force the hand of the heroine when she wants to come back home (by using force to get her to follow him), crack a rape-joke and explain her that no woman can resist him in the span of 3 pages. Let me tell you that it took me less than two sentences to despise him.<br><br>5) <b>The male-lead is an indifferent, grumpy asshole, and my only satisfaction comes from the fact that Ophélie, the MC, doesn't love him</b>. GOOD. I could have done without her crazy interpretation of his actions, though, even if it made for a good laugh : this guy, who put her in harm way and did NOTHING to prevent her from being the naive and stupid girl she stays during the whole book, finally tells her that, I quote (well, I translate, lol), <i>"he was starting to get used to her"</i>. <br><br>And then she thinks that he is falling in love with her. <br><br>What.<br><br>The.<br><br>Fuck. <br><br>I don't know about you, but I get used to annoyances. I do not "get used" to people I love. REALLY GIRL. <br><br><b>All the characters are caricatural</b> and this is a shame because the world had potential, but the characters (and the fact that NOTHING HAPPENS) completely spoiled my read. <br><br>As ecstatic as I was to finally read a Fantasy YA novel written in French, and despite the NUMEROUS praises it got in France (I mean, it's published by GALLIMARD!), I cannot, for the life of me, recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18043539.Les_Fianc_s_de_l_hiver" title="Les Fiancés de l'hiver by Christelle Dabos" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Fiancés de l'hiver</a> and I would never put it in a teenager's hands.<br><br><b>They deserve better than poor characterization and sexist stereotypes. Just nope.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468376056i/19698043._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cela faisait si longtemps que j'attendais de mettre les mains sur ce livre que je ne peux m'empêcher d'être profondément déçue par ce que je viens de lire. Alors c'est ça, le fameux livre de Fantasy qui a reçu tant d'éloges? Sérieusement? <b>La littérature française mérite mieux.</b><br><br>Comme je l'ai expliqué dans ma première partie, j'ai été tout d'abord extrêmement choquée par les relents sexistes véhiculés par <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18043539.Les_Fianc_s_de_l_hiver" title="Les Fiancés de l'hiver by Christelle Dabos" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Fiancés de l'hiver</a>. Moi qui m'attendais à une société matriarcale, je reste sans voix face à tous les stéréotypes genrés : <br><br>1) Peu importe la manière dont on nous le présente, <b>la naïveté d'Ophélie, si agaçante en soi pour la bonne marche de l'histoire, se fait également l'alliée d'une représentation de la société complètement obsolète et, pour moi, dangereuse</b> : <br><br>- Passe encore qu'elle doive subir un mariage forcé, je suis prête à accepter qu'il s'agisse d'une tradition dans le monde créé par <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7123624.Christelle_Dabos" title="Christelle Dabos" rel="nofollow noopener">Christelle Dabos</a>. <b>Rien par contre ne justifie le fait qu'Ophélie se montre si passive tout au long de l'histoire, ni que toutes les femmes qu'elle côtoie - mis à part sa tante - soient présentées comme des garces (je cite) ou des frivoles sans aucun intérêt</b>. S'il y a quelque chose que je déteste, c'est quand on me force à apprécier une héroïne en essayant de me faire croire que sa "pureté" équivaut à ce qu'une femme se doit d'être. Non, juste NON. <br><br>Ce slut-shaming éhonté me donne envie de vomir.<br><br>- <b>Parlons de la vision que ce livre véhicule du sexe, ok?</b> Donc nous nous adressons à des adolescent(e)s, d'accord? Il me semble dangereux de renforcer cette vision si courante du sexe comme quelque chose de sale, mauvais, et foncièrement réservé aux femmes de "petite vertu". Franchement, en 2016, je suis abasourdie de trouver encore ce genre de conneries. Attention, je ne suis pas en train de dire que les livres pour adolescents devraient être remplis de scènes de sexe, non, mais il y a un juste milieu entre un roman érotique et cette manière presque religieuse de l'aborder. <b>Une représentation saine du sexe ne l'associe pas un "pêché" presque biblique. Une représentation saine du sexe montre des partenaires consentants, et ne le diabolise pas ainsi.</b> Parce que vraiment, à part des scènes d'adultères où la femme est systématiquement montrée du doigt (l'homme, lui, n'a rien à se reprocher, je suppose?), que présente t-on à Ophélie? Rien. <br><br>- Parlons-en, tiens, d'Ophélie. <b>J'ai trouvé très dérangeant que cette adolescente de 17 ans (je suppose?) soit caractérisée d'une manière si enfantine</b>. Je ne sais pas si cela vient de sa "personnalité" (encore fût-il qu'elle en ait une) ou du style d'écriture, mais je n'ai jamais eu l'impression de suivre les aventures d'une jeune fille. Son extrême naïveté, sa propension à subir ce qui lui arrive m'a profondément agacée, et ce même si elle se rebellait dans sa tête. Ce n'est pas suffisant. Alors d'accord, elle a légèrement évolué en fin d'histoire, mais franchement, pas assez pour que cela n'ait un impact vraiment positif. <br><br>2) <b>Tous les personnages sont caricaturaux et n'ont aucune dimension</b>. Alors vous avez la mère d'Ophélie, plus excessive qu'une héroïne de Vaudeville ; Thorn, le rustre sans saveur qui, tout héros qu'il est, doit pondre 15 phrases en 400 pages ; Archibald, le connard qui trouve ça amusant de blaguer sur le fait qu'il pourrait prendre sa virginité s'il le souhaitait (parce que quand même, lui sait séduire, vous savez) ; Berenilde, la manipulatrice amoureuse prête à tout pour garder l'élu de son cœur ; la famille de Thorn, les méchants, vraiment très méchants, très méchants. <br><br>Pfffff. J'en peux plus de ces gens. Donnez moi des nuances, faites moi croire en vos personnages. Ces marionnettes en papier mâché ont cessé de m'amuser bien trop vite. <br><br>3) Franchement, il ne se passe rien. C'est d'un ennuyeux! Passé les premières pages, engageantes et intrigantes, <b>l'action stagne et s'il se passe des choses, l'histoire en soi n'avance pas vraiment, pas assez en tout cas au bout de 400 pages.</b> <br><br>4) <b>Le style d'écriture est maladroit</b>, alternant une syntaxe simple avec un vocabulaire parfois désuet, le tout extrêmement juvénile. Et ne me parlez pas des dialogues, qui sonnent si faux que je n'ai jamais réussi à m'immerger complètement dans les interactions des personnages. <br><br>5) <b>Quant au monde décrit, je dois reconnaitre que je l'ai trouvé fascinant, et c'est ce qui me rend si triste</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18043539.Les_Fianc_s_de_l_hiver" title="Les Fiancés de l'hiver by Christelle Dabos" rel="nofollow noopener">Les Fiancés de l'hiver</a> avait tant, tant de potentiel. Les animistes, le Pole, tout était là pour nous entrainer dans une histoire fantastique, et le résultat me fait l'effet d'un pétard mouillé. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517072759" />
    <a title="Kylie D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80033559-kylie-d"><img alt="Kylie D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527289322p2/80033559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2517072759?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kylie D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kylie D" href="/user/show/80033559-kylie-d">Kylie D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925603828" href="/book/show/40723006-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=seasonal-challenges">seasonal-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80033559-kylie-d?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2517072759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8227712598007234809">A novel that takes place in a world so similar, yet different, to our own. God has gotten angry and smashed the world into little pieces. It sees Ophelia travel to a distant ark, as these fragments of the world are now called, for an arranged marriage to Thorn, the Pole ark's treasurer. <br/><br/>Ophelia has certain gifts, just by touching an object she can read the feelings and mindset of people who have previously touched that object, and she also has the ability to travel through mirrors. Yet others ha</span>
  <span id="freeText8227712598007234809" style="display:none">A novel that takes place in a world so similar, yet different, to our own. God has gotten angry and smashed the world into little pieces. It sees Ophelia travel to a distant ark, as these fragments of the world are now called, for an arranged marriage to Thorn, the Pole ark's treasurer. <br /><br />Ophelia has certain gifts, just by touching an object she can read the feelings and mindset of people who have previously touched that object, and she also has the ability to travel through mirrors. Yet others have more powerful abilities and she fails to see why someone as insignificant as herself has been requested as Thorn's wife. She finds that people on the Pole ark aren't always as they seem, some she trusted will try to betray her, but she also finds some unexpected allies. What follows is a tale of political intrigue, manipulation and secrets as Ophelia finds that the truth is scarier than she first thought, and those around her find her stronger than she looks.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book, whipping through it in a couple of sessions. Christelle Dabos weaves an amazing tale, through rich settings and characters This is the first book in The Mirror Visitor series, and I'll definitely be on the lookout for the rest of the series as they become available. A first rate fantasy book.<br /><br />My thanks to Text Publishing for a copy to read and review. The opinions are all my own.</span>

<div id="review_2534700853" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534700853" />
    <a title="Umut Rados" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados"><img alt="Umut Rados" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576844432p2/24816039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2534700853?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Umut Rados" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Umut Rados" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados">Umut Rados</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781609454838" href="/book/show/39724529-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2534700853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4208423408558856946">I really enjoyed the book. The world was so imaginative and creative. I truly loved the setting. It was also simple enough that made it even easier to grasp and enjoy. Probably Ophelia was the best part of this book for me. It was a powerful character development, and a very likeable heroine. She was very pragmatic in the way she approached the events. There was lots of court politics and relationship management. Dabos managed to create a strong intrigue. I kept turning the pages to learn why on</span>
  <span id="freeText4208423408558856946" style="display:none">I really enjoyed the book. The world was so imaginative and creative. I truly loved the setting. It was also simple enough that made it even easier to grasp and enjoy. Probably Ophelia was the best part of this book for me. It was a powerful character development, and a very likeable heroine. She was very pragmatic in the way she approached the events. There was lots of court politics and relationship management. Dabos managed to create a strong intrigue. I kept turning the pages to learn why on earth Ophelia was in Pole, what was happening in Pole, who are all these people, what will happen in the end? I found the writing very simple and enjoyable. The World building was very clever. In some fantasy books, it becomes so complicated that you give up. Or, it’s just not creative enough, a prince, a princess, and an expected romance. However, I found A Winter’s Promise very original.<br />The only criticism I have for the book is the dragging in the middle when Ophelia arrives to Pole, and tries to get to know people. The relationships, the court dynamics took too long to settle in my opinion. It’s a classic pit hole in fantasy books, and unfortunately Dabos couldn’t escape this as well.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed the book. If you’re looking for an original and creative world set up, this is a very good option. Heroine is definitely resourceful and very likeable. Writing is fluid and imaginative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4208423408558856946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2070312570" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2070312570" />
    <a title="Sophia." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6520961-sophia"><img alt="Sophia." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322479535p2/6520961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2070312570?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia." href="/user/show/6520961-sophia">Sophia.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=confusing">confusing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=deja-vu">deja-vu</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=eye-rolls-and-frowning">eye-rolls-and-frowning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=too-many-repetitions">too-many-repetitions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=unbelievable">unbelievable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=annoying-narrator">annoying-narrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=useless-and-ineffective">useless-and-ineffective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6520961-sophia?shelf=twilightesque">twilightesque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2070312570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9717610400430423098">If you read a lot of Y.A. literature, this book will seem vaguely familiar to you. That’s because it just borrows a bunch of ideas from the most popular books out there. Harry Potter, Shadow and Bone (for a clueless girl thrown into a royal court), Vampire Diaries, too (Ambassador Archibald is a carbon copy of Adrian Ivashkov, or more accurately, a less charismatic version of him), and so many more I can’t be bothered to remember. The whole story is just a washed-out copy of those books. <br/><br/>Everyon</span>
  <span id="freeText9717610400430423098" style="display:none">If you read a lot of Y.A. literature, this book will seem vaguely familiar to you. That’s because it just borrows a bunch of ideas from the most popular books out there. Harry Potter, Shadow and Bone (for a clueless girl thrown into a royal court), Vampire Diaries, too (Ambassador Archibald is a carbon copy of Adrian Ivashkov, or more accurately, a less charismatic version of him), and so many more I can’t be bothered to remember. The whole story is just a washed-out copy of those books. <br /><br />Everyone is super flat and one-dimensional. The bad guys are very mean, the good guys are very kind. It’s obvious that Ophélie and Thorn are going to end up loving each other. But you know what? I couldn’t bring myself to care, because Thorn doesn’t feel real. He’s too “cold” to be genuine. Can you seriously imagine someone like him? Nobody felt real. They’re just caricatures. The dialogues were awkward, nobody talks like that either. And could anyone really picture what the Family Spirits looked like? These descriptions were terrible. <br /><br />The writing was really clumsy. The first chapters were very good (probably because they were carefully edited and polished) but that’s about it. Sometimes I even couldn’t understand what Ophélie was feeling or trying to say. I just had to stop to read the sentences over and over again and they still didn’t make any sense. A couple of times I actually went back and re-read the previous page to try to understand where she was coming from ! She would jump to conclusions that had strictly no correlation to what she was saying beforehand, or her feelings (especially when Thorn was concerned) were just hard to follow because she would change her mind every other page. <br /><br />Also, sooo many repetitions. Here’s how it is: the author gives a defining trait to each character. And she doesn’t want you to forget those assigned traits so she kindly reminds you every.single.time.they.talk. Berenilde is gorgeous and has tattoos. Ophélie has “heavy dark curls” (how many times does she say those exact words??) The aunt has "horse-like teeth". All of these are repeated a hundred times throughout the book, the most important one being….. Thorn is tall, y’all. I am not kidding, every single time Ophélie looked at him, she HAD to say something about how much of a giant he is, how tall his legs are, how gigantic he is, how small she is compared to how tall he is, because he is a giant, and when she borrows his coat it's so huge because he's so tall and she's so small, and how she gets dizzy just looking at him because she’s so short and he’s so freakishly tall, because, you know, he’s a giant and he’s skinny but did you know that he is also very tall?.... I GET IT! It got exasperating. <br /><br />It’s the same for Ophélie though. The author learned her lesson from reading so many YA books: readers don’t like perfect, Mary Sue characters. Fine. But honestly Ophélie is so flawed that it’s laughable. She has zero redeeming qualities. None. She’s clumsly to the point of foolishness, she's not pretty, she’s socially awkward, she isn't funny, sassy or sarcastic, she’s not interesting in the least, she’s not smart, she’s not a fast-learner, she’s always sneezing, falling, or being passive and clueless as to what is going on around her. She doesn’t care about her hair and has poor personal hygiene (she doesn’t bathe for a week and that’s fine by her), she doesn’t care about being feminine and/or trying to improve her appearance because that’s for slutty girls like her sister (rolls eyes), she doesn’t care about her clothes (she wears mismatched shoes and grandmother’s clothes etc.), she doesn’t care about guys, and she’s sick throughout the entire book. Meaning she has a cold during the entire storyline. Is that supposed to make her relatable? I have never, ever read a book where so many of the heroine’s interactions with other characters are punctuated by regulars “Ophélie stopped talking to sneeze. She blew her nose three times.” She's a complete tool. Even Bella Swan was more lively. That’s saying something. Come on, get a grip girl! I felt nothing towards her but annoyance. Yet, everyone is just obsessed with her and she seems to be the key to saving everyone. ROLLS EYES.<br /><br />Also, she’s so annoying because she consistently made poor decisions and refused what her allies advised her to do. When Berenilde tortures her and Thorn asks her about it, she chooses not to tell him, for reasons that are eerily similar to Harry Potter’s when he was being tortured by Dolores Umbridge. Although in Ophélie’s case, it's just stupid and doesn’t make any sense. He could help you, you idiot! <br /><br />And the mission! So they're a group planning to infiltrate the royal court by disguising their true identities, which will obviously require fake names and very careful planning. The stakes are high, they're risking their lives if they're discovered. Days before they effectively penetrate the court, Ophélie disobeys direct orders of staying put because she's an idiot, and her stupid wandering around leads her to getting lost, obviously, because she's a tool. She ends up running into a prince from the actual court THEY ARE TRYING TO INFILTRATE and she's thick enough to babble away valuable information. THEN, when she gets back, she never mentions to her teammates that she’s met Archibald, NOT ONCE, even though he is bound to recognize her for who she really is when they do infiltrate! Her silence literally jeopardized everyone and the entire mission altogether! Does she have a good reason for doing that and acting like a complete cretin? No. But does she at least feel guilty and realize that her complete foolishness put everyone in deadly danger? Also no. <br /><br />And when Berenilde specifically tells her “Listen, this is important, Gustave is going to approach you with an offer, tell me at once when he does” what does she do when Gustave indeed approaches her? NOTHING. Does she warn Berenilde? OF COURSE NOT. I swear she’s dumber than a goat. <br /><br />And I know her marriage was arranged but since she had no other option than to just, well, roll with it, I got annoyed at how she refused to try and work with Thorn. You’re bound to the guy. You have no choice so why not try to make the best of it? He’s not THAT bad. He watches out for you. Stop being so immature and try to make this situation that you’ve been given a better one. <br /><br />Ugh. The overall reading experience felt very childish. The world building was okay, but I liked Anima better than the Pole. Honestly my two-stars are for the scarf, because that was freaking cute. Forget about the rest. The whole book is just so goddamn dull.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9717610400430423098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April (Aprilius Maximus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April (Aprilius Maximus)" href="/user/show/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus">April (Aprilius Maximus)</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20658145-april-aprilius-maximus?shelf=2018">2018</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2487415882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5785011368842260984">DNF'd on page 185/491.<br/><br/>Thank you so much to Text Publishing Australia for sending a copy of this to me! Unfortunately, I just couldn't get into it. The first chapter was so promising, with so much atmosphere and it had it's own distinct, magical vibe that made me think I was going to love this book! However, as I kept reading, I kept encountering more and more problems. For example, on page 49, <i>"A nanny pushed a pram while blushing at the admiring whistles of workmen up scaffolding." </i> Ughhhhh why</span>
  <span id="freeText5785011368842260984" style="display:none">DNF'd on page 185/491.<br /><br />Thank you so much to Text Publishing Australia for sending a copy of this to me! Unfortunately, I just couldn't get into it. The first chapter was so promising, with so much atmosphere and it had it's own distinct, magical vibe that made me think I was going to love this book! However, as I kept reading, I kept encountering more and more problems. For example, on page 49, <i>"A nanny pushed a pram while blushing at the admiring whistles of workmen up scaffolding." </i> Ughhhhh why are we insinuating that this is a normal thing, that women should blush when disgusting men do this. ALSO I thought this was a children's book, so I was super upset that lines like this were used without being challenged, but as I read more and more of the book, I realised this is certainly NOT a children's book. <br />We have another character calling a woman a slut just because she was sleeping with her brother and we have another character who ... ugh... let me just show you..<br /><i>Archibald finally let out a deep sigh. "I'll admit to you that I'm a little disappointed. It would have been frightfully amusing to have Thorn's betrothed at my disposal."<br />"And why's that?" she asked, frowning.<br />"Well, to deflower her, of course."</i><br />LIKE..... SERIOUSLY?<br />I'm just done with this book. The storyline itself isn't even interesting enough for me to continue with it and the main characters are EXTREMELY bland. <br />SUPER BUMMED.</span>

<div id="review_2827011173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2827011173" />
    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2827011173?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2827011173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer275393457207822207">4****<br/>A great reread! I loved the world and enjoyed the characters of Ophelia, Foster and Gail. Might have to reread the second book now.<br/><br/>Original review:<br/>That was really interesting and a rather unusual fantasy book to what I usually read! Long ago there was a cataclysm called The Rupture and the world split its lands into celestial floating islands, known as Arks. Over each, the spirit of an immortal ancestor abides- they ere said to be the survivors of the rupture. Due to the Rupture, each Ark h</span>
  <span id="freeText275393457207822207" style="display:none">4****<br />A great reread! I loved the world and enjoyed the characters of Ophelia, Foster and Gail. Might have to reread the second book now.<br /><br />Original review:<br />That was really interesting and a rather unusual fantasy book to what I usually read! Long ago there was a cataclysm called The Rupture and the world split its lands into celestial floating islands, known as Arks. Over each, the spirit of an immortal ancestor abides- they ere said to be the survivors of the rupture. Due to the Rupture, each Ark has strict rules regarding marriage and reproduction. In addition, each Ark is known for its own power- each one unique and different. <br /><br />Ophelia is an Anima with the specific gift of being able to read the emotions, thoughts, and scenes of objects belonging to past owners. She is extremely powerful at this, being one of the few who were actually trained to develop their power further. She also has the ability to be able to travel through mirrors. Ophelia is head-strong but soft spoken and loves her job in a museum here she can read the past items if she wishes to. Unlike her family members, she is not interested in appearances and couldn't care less about marriage or reproducing.<br /><br />However, her simple life is soon upturned when she is told she HAS to marry a man from a far off, not-well-known land. As declining the marriage would mean banishment and family shame, Ophelia has to leave behind her family and much loved museum to the cold ark known as the Pole and follow her fiancee to the Citaceleste, the Capital. Here things are not as they seem and Ophelia is unable to trust anybody.<br /><br />Armed with her quiet bravery, her curiosity and listening skills, Ophelia is able to uncover the truth and a larger political purpose to her marriage is at play. Ophelia is treated dreadfully by those in the Citaceleste however she does meet very few she can trust. The people of this place are manipulative and proud, and their customs are completely different to what Ophelia is use to. She is unlucky in the sense that she clearly does not feel comfortable and does not belong there and mean/terrible things seem to be directed to toward her.<br /><br />Ophelia was a great character, despite myself thinking that she needs to say something-speak her mind, we do have a character who has a quiet form of bravery and endures much pain. It was interesting to read how the author created a world where the social norms seem quite different from my own. You couldn't help but feel sorry for Ophelia as she is faced with an arranged marriage that she just doesn't want, and she is at odds with the other women in her family and those from the Pole who only seem to care for appearances and social standing. <br /><br />This book as probably more of a 3.5*** rounded up. This book is not constant action, but instead, rather introspective from Ophelia's POV. This focused more on the world building and understanding the powers and manipulations of others, so some parts of the book did seem to drag. However, overall I did enjoy this novel and I am going to read the second book to find out what happens next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="275393457207822207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2517313592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517313592" />
    <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf"><img alt="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540171256p2/9185509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2517313592?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)" href="/user/show/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf">Melissa (Mel’s Bookshelf)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925603828" href="/book/show/40723006-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9185509-melissa-mel-s-bookshelf?shelf=fantasy-ya">fantasy-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2517313592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5368784377932713756">4.25 Stars.<br/>I really enjoyed this YA debut novel by French author Christelle Dabos. It has won numerous awards in Europe so it was no surprise that it has recently finally been translated into English. I don't read many translated books and was excited to give this one a go! I have read some wonderful reviews about the French version. I wanted to see what sort of atmosphere it had. It did not disappoint!<br/><br/>In a unique universe, the world has been smashed up into different "arks". Ophelia is a young </span>
  <span id="freeText5368784377932713756" style="display:none">4.25 Stars.<br>I really enjoyed this YA debut novel by French author Christelle Dabos. It has won numerous awards in Europe so it was no surprise that it has recently finally been translated into English. I don't read many translated books and was excited to give this one a go! I have read some wonderful reviews about the French version. I wanted to see what sort of atmosphere it had. It did not disappoint!<br><br>In a unique universe, the world has been smashed up into different "arks". Ophelia is a young woman living on Anima. She has the ability to travel short distances through mirrors and can also read objects histories by touch. When against her wishes she is betrothed to a man on another Ark, Ophelia has to leave her secure and loving home and travel to a cold and desolate ark to marry him. Thorn is a powerful man, and has many enemies who will stop at nothing to see his and his future wife's demise.<br><br>I have read a few reviews commenting on the misogyny A Winter's Promise and its characters. While I agree, yes there is a lot of it, I must say I took it differently than a lot of those reviewers. I believe it is a story of a young woman finding her power in such a landscape and navigating her way through it. I feel like the story line has a purpose. And I feel it will take much more than one book to get there. The scene is set, and yes it's depressing to be a woman in this book, especially Ophelia. But there are three more books coming, and I am really excited to see how strong she becomes, and how she can change her world for the better.<br><br>Honestly I didn't find it any more misogynistic than 99.9% of the other YA books I have read. The most popular YA franchises generally have the mistreatment of women as a theme.  If a YA book can bring this to light I am all for it, provided there is an adequate resolution of the story line and at least permits young readers to recognise the issues and feel inspired to change their own world.<br><br>It reminded me a lot of The Selection, and The Red Queen series in certain ways, but I really disliked those series, I don't really like books that deal with competing for a man's love. I found The Mirror Visitor to be much more encouraging. She doesn't even want to be with the 'hero' of the book, and has so many other strengths going for her than the love of a man, and I think that is made perfectly clear.<br><br>The author has created such a unique and expansive world for her characters. I absolutely loved reading about the scenery and what on earth she was going to get herself into next! It had so many twists and turns! I found getting through this book extremely easy, completing it in just three sittings.<br><br>I liked the characters even more than I was expecting, even Thorn I gradually warmed to slightly by the end, even though he was a grump of a character. I can't wait to find out more about him in subsequent books!<br><br>It ends in a MAJOR cliffhanger, but I really want to read what happens next!<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539530179i/26448108._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="A Winter's Promise" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Would I Recommend A Winter's Promise?</b><br>It was fun. Pure YA entertainment. Because it was translated from French it had a very unique vibe to it which I can only imagine is due to the authors background and talent. It was eerie and imaginative, detailed and the universe was so expansive! I thoroughly enjoyed it and imagine most fans of YA will feel the same way.<br><br><i>Many thanks to Text Publishing for a copy of A Winter's Promise to review.</i><br><br>For more reviews check out my<br><a href="http://www.melsbookshelf.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a><br><a href="http://www.facebook.com/melsbookshelfAU" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a><br><a href="http://www.instagram.com/mels_book_shelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br><a href="http://www.twitter.com/melsbookshelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5368784377932713756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2484798542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484798542" />
    <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer"><img alt="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553042105p2/7476091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484798542?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer">Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40969531-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-a-magic">g-a-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=fiction-young-adult">fiction-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-a-strong-family">g-a-strong-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-suspenseful">imo-suspenseful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=review-wrote-add-later">review-wrote-add-later</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=stars-5">stars-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-worthy-love-interest">imo-worthy-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-c-morally-grey">g-c-morally-grey</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484798542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16319590588604824513"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524545682i/25424812._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='257' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href='https://perspectiveofawriter.com/category/book-reviews/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br/><br/>Long ago, a cataclysm shattered the world into many floating celestial islands. These Arks, have each developed in distinct ways, possessing its own unique relationship to time. Beneath her worn scarf and thick glasses, Ophelia hides the ability to read and communicate with the souls of objects, and the power to travel through mirrors. Her peaceful existence on the Ark of Anima is disrupted when she is promised in marriage to Thorn, from the po</span>
  <span id="freeText16319590588604824513" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1524545682i/25424812._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="257" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Check out more reviews @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.com/category/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>...</i><br><br>Long ago, a cataclysm shattered the world into many floating celestial islands. These Arks, have each developed in distinct ways, possessing its own unique relationship to time. Beneath her worn scarf and thick glasses, Ophelia hides the ability to read and communicate with the souls of objects, and the power to travel through mirrors. Her peaceful existence on the Ark of Anima is disrupted when she is promised in marriage to Thorn, from the powerful Dragon clan. Ophelia must follow her fiancée to the floating capital on the distant Ark of the Pole. Why has she been chosen? Why must she hide her true identity? Though she doesn’t know it yet, she’s become a pawn in a deadly plot.<br><br><b>The short review...</b><br><br>Some readers would probably fight me on the fact that I wasn't loving this at 24% and yet I still gave A Winter's Promise 5 stars... Well that is because it was the perfect setup for a story I didn't expect and which in hindsight needed that 24% to give us a feel for Ophelia. <br><br>Ophelia is NOT an adventurer. She is NOT badass. She is not cool, neat and no one can claim she is a special snowflake!!! Ophelia is a museum curator. She is responsible in the same way an absent minded professor is, that is dedicated to their work and otherwise floating through life, not worrying much about material possessions, lovers or appearances. <br><br>Then she is thrust into the most incredible of worlds!!!! Can you imagine?! Well that world doesn't appear until 25%! But we HAD to see what kind of person Ophelia is and what her circumstances are and the horrible situation she is thrust into... that took 24%. This is actually quite a tight setup, some books take upwards of 40 to 50% (and I could name quite a few hyped books that do...) so really A Winter's Promise gets underway and once it does I'm drawn right into Thorn's world... The world that Ophelia must navigate otherwise she won't survive to see herself married.<br><br>So what is this world like?! Well... it seems like a rather old-fashioned world at first... Ophelia is forced by her family to marry this man who for all intents and purposes lives on the moon! She has no idea what to expect and her fiancee does NOT enlighten her. We get the sense right off that Thorn is not going to be a man who makes you swoon because he knows how to treat a woman... No in fact Ophelia realizes quickly that she will have to rely on herself. It is quite a modern treatment for what starts out with an old-fashioned idea. I came to really appreciate how he relied on Ophelia being a capable young woman who is no slouch in his politically pitfalled world. <br><br>I won't say much more because as the book opens up, like Ophelia, you come to understand how life at the Pole works. It's political, about illusion and appearances (being the opposite of what you expect) and no one is safe! In fact, every single person she meets is morally grey, thank goodness her godmother came with her! There are no easy fixes (no one has answers for her) and yet Ophelia does come to find some allies... <br><br>This is the first book of a series... so it ends at a pivotal point, but it is clearly just the beginning. We've gotten the best start, a well thought out solid one, that will serve us well through the entire series... and the slow burn on this romance is so realistic and raw that I can't help rooting for Thorn and Ophelia even though he is more a real man with all the flaws than most book boyfriends. This is a world that I want to get even more deliciously complex and strange... And I want to see Ophelia continue to grow and come into her own as a woman of action!<br> <br><br><b>Cover &amp; Title grade -&gt; A+</b><br><br>I LOVE the cover... That is what attracted me to it at the first, it sold the premise and it didn't disappoint as I read. I loved that I got an idea of what the setting looked like from the cover. And I love that the other covers in the series follow the same solid color with ink drawing of a location pattern that is established with A Winter's Promise. I NEED this series on my book shelf! <br><br><br><b>What are a couple of the many highlights in A Winter's Promise?</b><br><br>-Mega Politics!<br>This is the dirty, underhanded, morally grey way politics should be done! There is social rivalry, warring clans and romantic scandals, oh my! It makes for a rather treacherous world to maneuver through and its NOT terribly action oriented though there are plenty of backstabby events and horrid situations instead...<br><br>-An Incredible World!<br>First off Archibald's castle, changing spaces, masterpiece of architecture is literally a place I WANT to visit! It is an embassy where the different rivals can come and not be killed off... only is it as safe as they say?! Well there are some magical things like taking rooms to their own spaces, that do a good job at maintaining safety but there are always ways to get around those features...<br><br>-All the Magic!<br>Thorn and his aunt Berenilde can flay Ophelia with their minds... And Archibald, the ambassador, is mentally connected to his family! There is another clan all about illusions, and Ophelia gets up close and personal with one magical outfit! It's all deliciously dangerous...<br><br><br><b>As a Writer...</b><br><br>One of the things I really appreciate about A Winter's Promise as a writer as well as a reader is her characters! <br><br>I've shared my loving adoration of Ophelia, but I'll say again that I love how she jumped into this world that is everything she is not and is dealing with it. She is not in her natural habitat and that is what made her so great...<br><br>I adore the cold and hard Thorn and his very subtle softening toward Ophelia. It doesn't happen swiftly and it isn't evident very much. He is a hard worker though and comes to respect Ophelia and that I really admire! The harder they are the more gooey they are inside... <br><br>Berenilde, hahahhahha, you won't know if she's you alley or your enemy! I did wonder at her incredible crush on their patriarch... It's a hard world that Thorn has lived in if this is his only ally...<br><br>I come to appreciate Ophelia's godmother as much as she does, when she continually is outraged for her nieces sake!<br><br>And there are so many more characters that will take you by surprise... Archibald, the architect, the mechanic, the servant that shows Ophelia the ropes, the Knight, Thorn's sister! GAHHHH! It's a lush, lush world with complex characters... Oh and I can't forget to mention Ophelia's scarf that is animated and lively like a squirmy pet!!<br><br>If you're looking for a heroine who decidedly DOES NOT want to fall for her fiancee, then you need Ophelia! If you want a heroine who is not gorgeous, scintillating and super talented then you need Ophelia, who has a couple gifts but with only rather limited uses... Yet she persists none-the-less! If you want a world that is an intriguing mix of politics, magic and back stabbers then you need A Winter's Promise!!<br><br><br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Authenticity<br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Writing Style<br>⋆ ⭐⭐⭐⭐ Plot &amp; Pacing<br>⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ World Building<br><br><i>Thanks to Edelweiss and the publisher for providing me with a copy in exchange for an honest review. It has not influenced my opinions.</i><br><br>______________________<br>You can find this review and many others on my book blog @ <a href="https://perspectiveofawriter.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Perspective of a Writer</a>. See my special perspective at the bottom of my reviews under the typewriter...<br><br><i>Please like this review if you enjoyed it! *bow* *bow* It helps me out a ton!!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16319590588604824513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6613045042182483064">Don't get the logic of comparing this book to N.K. Jemisin's in the blurb. To me, the style was more reminiscent of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28194.Inkheart__Inkworld___1_' title='Inkheart (Inkworld, #1) by Cornelia Funke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Inkheart</a>.<br/><br/>Not my thing.<br/><br/>P.S. Sampling and abandoning is great! Everyone should do more of it, IMO.</span>
  <span id="freeText6613045042182483064" style="display:none">Don't get the logic of comparing this book to N.K. Jemisin's in the blurb. To me, the style was more reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28194.Inkheart__Inkworld___1_" title="Inkheart (Inkworld, #1) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkheart</a>.<br /><br />Not my thing.<br /><br />P.S. Sampling and abandoning is great! Everyone should do more of it, IMO.</span>

<div id="review_2800634545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText16476892490969180274" style="display:none">DNF at page 113!<br /><br />I'm not having much luck with my reading recently, A Winter's Promise was disappointing for me personally as I had high hopes for a new, popular fantasy read. The part that ultimately made me decide to DNF was a remark made about the main character's weight. This was said in a way that was similar to when I used to get bullied for my appearance. <div id="review_2616477103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616477103" />
    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80389896-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535926266p2/80389896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2616477103?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/80389896-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925603828" href="/book/show/40723006-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616477103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1944938197656517329">Man that went downhill quickly. <br/><br/>It started out a 4 star, but ended up being up horrible. <br/><br/> I'll admit, the first fifty or so pages were amazing, and I wished it had stayed on that track, because the second they got to Citaceleste, things were BAD. <br/><br/>At first I really liked ophelia. I thought she was the right mix of smart and quirky and stubborn to make her akin to the protagonists of the middle grade books I used to read voraciously. The first fifty or so pages were similar to the Mysterious Bened</span>
  <span id="freeText1944938197656517329" style="display:none">Man that went downhill quickly. <br /><br />It started out a 4 star, but ended up being up horrible. <br /><br /> I'll admit, the first fifty or so pages were amazing, and I wished it had stayed on that track, because the second they got to Citaceleste, things were BAD. <br /><br />At first I really liked ophelia. I thought she was the right mix of smart and quirky and stubborn to make her akin to the protagonists of the middle grade books I used to read voraciously. The first fifty or so pages were similar to the Mysterious Benedict Society for me, only with an older feel, but it turned out to be completely different than the first fifty pages and GOD AM I UPSET. <br /><br />There seemed to be no point to this book. The plot was unclear and odd, taking twists and turned whenever the author pleased. Once I thought it was about this thing, something else would take the stage. <br /><br />All of the characters in Citaceleste were pretentious and dull. Enough said. <br /><br />I expected an enchanting novel about people with the ability to read objects, their histories, and so on. I wanted to learn about mirror travel. Instead I got a hot royal mess featuring fatphobia, borderline incest, and magic that, even for magic, makes no hecking sense. <br /><br />I knew once Archibald showed up and joked about taking advantage of Ophelia things weren't going to be good. I should've called it quits right then. <br /><br />Dont be fooled by the pretty cover and intriguing premise. This is not a good read. <br /><br />*drops mic*<br /><br /> Peace out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1944938197656517329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2937047230" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47188780-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520288810p2/47188780.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2937047230?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/47188780-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39986039-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2937047230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16668216095904732030">Best French Fantasy Novel and Best French Young Adult Novel 2014. Dabos’ fantasy series is filled with magic, illusion, and intrigue. Ophelia has certain gifts—she can experience an object’s history through touch (i.e., a ‘reader’) and she can travel through mirrors. She enjoyed her work as a museum curator before her family arranged for her to be married to Thorn. She has to travel to a different Ark [arks are a series of floating islands that formed when the world broke apart].<br/><br/>Ophelia is thrus</span>
  <span id="freeText16668216095904732030" style="display:none">Best French Fantasy Novel and Best French Young Adult Novel 2014. Dabos’ fantasy series is filled with magic, illusion, and intrigue. Ophelia has certain gifts—she can experience an object’s history through touch (i.e., a ‘reader’) and she can travel through mirrors. She enjoyed her work as a museum curator before her family arranged for her to be married to Thorn. She has to travel to a different Ark [arks are a series of floating islands that formed when the world broke apart].<br /><br />Ophelia is thrust into a world of intrigue and danger as Thorn’s fiancé. The twisting plot introduces us to a plethora of characters that all seem to have special powers. Ophelia learns to become more determined and independent; and begins to use her own powers with increasing self-assurance. As for the Treasurer of the realm Thorn, there are hints that he may be more than the rigid, emotionless man that he presents to the world.<br /><br />I am totally ‘hooked’ and look forward to the next offering in this four-book series—“for beneath illusion is truth”. Recommend.</span>

<div id="review_2483487914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483487914" />
    <a title="Jessica Woodbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4271946-jessica-woodbury"><img alt="Jessica Woodbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415105097p2/4271946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483487914?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Woodbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Woodbury" href="/user/show/4271946-jessica-woodbury">Jessica Woodbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40969531-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=arc-provided-by-publisher">arc-provided-by-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483487914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7059316213901013659">I was intrigued by this book, Europa Editions publishing a YA Fantasy series was an interesting surprise, but then I held off reading it for a long time. I don't actually *like* much YA Fantasy and I have a hard time committing to a series. In the end, though, I really enjoyed this and it was a nice antidote to a bit of a reading slump where nothing was really doing it for me, which is a high compliment indeed.<br/><br/>Worldbuilding in Fantasy is a real tightrope walk, you have to create a complex world </span>
  <span id="freeText7059316213901013659" style="display:none">I was intrigued by this book, Europa Editions publishing a YA Fantasy series was an interesting surprise, but then I held off reading it for a long time. I don't actually *like* much YA Fantasy and I have a hard time committing to a series. In the end, though, I really enjoyed this and it was a nice antidote to a bit of a reading slump where nothing was really doing it for me, which is a high compliment indeed.<br /><br />Worldbuilding in Fantasy is a real tightrope walk, you have to create a complex world but you also have to be able to tell the characters' story without constantly explaining that complex world. The strange future Dabos creates with floating "ark" cities each with their own elaborate societies walked that line very well for me. Our protagonist Ophelia is sent to the Pole, and much of the joy of the book is getting to explore that strange world through her eyes. The extravagant world of the Pole is topsy-turvy, where you cannot believe what you see or what anyone tells you. Even when you feel a little more rooted in understanding the world, you never lose that precarious feeling that anything could change at any moment and that no one is quite what they seem. That's what this book does best and it's what I enjoyed the most.<br /><br />The writing style reminded me more of the older books I read growing up, classic more than contemporary prose. I appreciated that this wasn't a book with a Very Special Protagonist, while Ophelia does have her unusual talents, they don't give her any special status at home or in her new world. Her entry into the wild and dramatic story she finds herself in appears to be mostly random (though who knows what we will learn in subsequent books in the series). She is not beautiful, nor is she the kind of person who thinks she is not beautiful but will actually become so after a makeover. She is sickly and clumsy, but as she is our protagonist she is of course stubborn and headstrong. (Take all this with whatever grains of salt you need to as I am not a regular YA Fantasy reader, so I'm not the best person to comment on how this is true to or varies from the genre in its current state.)<br /><br />This book managed to throw twist after twist at me without leaving me feeling manipulated or annoyed, which is largely a result of the rules Dabos has built into the narrative. We expect these turns and we know another could be around any corner. While I'm not someone who commits to fantasy series (or really any series) very easily, I finished this book ready to pick up the second one immediately. Europa has officially got me addicted to a quartet for a second time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7059316213901013659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
