<div id="review_2885358282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2885358282" />
    <a title="Laurie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11248174-laurie"><img alt="Laurie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489588979p2/11248174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2885358282?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie" href="/user/show/11248174-laurie">Laurie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13178935274116793908">Like a steampunk Howl's Moving Castle meets Pride & Prejudice. But also completely unique (one of the most original fantasies since Laini Taylor's work). Fabulous. Highly recommended. </span>
  <span id="freeText13178935274116793908" style="display:none">Like a steampunk Howl's Moving Castle meets Pride &amp; Prejudice. But also completely unique (one of the most original fantasies since Laini Taylor's work). Fabulous. Highly recommended. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2522680818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2522680818" />
    <a title="Tammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3118961-tammy"><img alt="Tammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517013119p2/3118961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2522680818?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/3118961-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40969531-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2522680818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5069279886357667243">I received this book for free from the Publisher in exchange for an honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.<strong>The nitty-gritty:</strong> Lots of potential, but unfortunately, this story was too problematic for my taste.<br/><br/>Well, I think you can tell by my rating that <em><strong>A Winter’s Promise</strong></em> just didn’t work for me. I had high hopes for this book, which is apparently a huge success in the author’s native country of France, and has just been translated into English and p</span>
  <span id="freeText5069279886357667243" style="display:none">I received this book for free from the Publisher in exchange for an honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.<strong>The nitty-gritty:</strong> Lots of potential, but unfortunately, this story was too problematic for my taste.<br /><br />Well, I think you can tell by my rating that <em><strong>A Winter’s Promise</strong></em> just didn’t work for me. I had high hopes for this book, which is apparently a huge success in the author’s native country of France, and has just been translated into English and published by Europa Editions. I suppose my lack of enjoyment, and in fact my horror at some of the content of the story, could boil down to the translation, or perhaps the French worldview is just radically different from my American upbringing. But whatever the reason, I had a very hard time finishing this book. At about the 200 page mark I was starting to get worried that I might never finish it, and seeing that I still had 300 pages to go, I finally decided to skim the remainder, something I don’t think I’ve <i>
  ever 
</i>done before. I’m afraid this review is going to be skewed towards the negative, because there wasn’t much I enjoyed about the story. I also think this might be a good time for a “list” review, as I feel it might be an easier way to cover all the things I want to talk about.<br /><br />But first, a quick recap of the story, just to set the stage. <em><strong>A Winter’s Promise</strong></em> takes place after a world altering event called the Rupture, when Earth shattered into pieces, leaving clumps of isolated floating islands called arks. Ophelia is a young girl who lives on an ark called Anima, where she is able to communicate with objects when she touches them. For political reasons, she is being forced to marry a stranger from another ark called the Pole, a cold and desolate land completely different from the one she has lived in all her life. Ophelia will have to leave her huge family in order to travel to the Pole, and she will probably never see them again.<br /><br />When her husband-to-be comes to Anima to escort her back to the Pole, Ophelia is shocked by his lack of warmth, his intimidating height, and his refusal to talk to her. She reluctantly leaves her home, accompanied by an aunt who will serve as chaperone, and on the journey she attempts to connect with her fiance, Thorn, with little success. When they arrive, things become worse, as Thorn makes it clear that Ophelia's arrival on the Pole is to be kept a secret for the time being. He also issues a stern warning to stay put inside and never leave the manor house, as the outside world would be too dangerous. As Ophelia gradually begins to realize that her impending marriage has far greater consequences than she was led to believe, she must search for the real reason she was chosen to marry Thorn.<br /><br />Sounds cool, right? The world-building has some great potential, and I do realize that this is only the first book in a series, but let’s go over some of the problems I had with this book:<br /><br /><strong>1. I cannot figure out what this book is trying to be.</strong> The writing style feels like a middle grade book, lots of exaggeration, exclamation points, and overly dramatic writing. Even the cover art <i>feels </i>middle grade to me, for some reason. However, this is certainly not MG, and I don’t think it’s even what we would consider YA here in America. The subject matter, which I’ll get to in a bit, is not something I’d ever recommend to anyone under the age of eighteen. I also want to point out that there is a big red sticker on my copy that says “Top 10 Fall ‘18 Kids Next List Pick,” so someone out there feels this should comfortably sit on a "Best of" list for kids.<br /><br /><strong>2. I did not like a single character in this book, except for one.</strong> Ophelia is a mousey, timid girl who hides behind her unruly hair and a thick pair of glasses, barely speaks above a whisper, and doesn’t show much backbone when faced with important decisions. For some strange reason, she is constantly blowing her nose, and the author makes sure to mention that each and every time. And although she seems shocked at some of the things the other characters say and do to her, she never puts up much of a fight. I get it. She’s an introvert, she works in a museum, and she doesn’t want to call attention to herself. In a way, this was a refreshing change from all the strong, independent female characters in most YA fiction, which is starting to feel like the norm. But I just wanted to scream at her to fight back, already!<br /><br />**Note: the one thing I did like about Ophelia is that I believe she is asexual, as she mentions more than once that she’s never felt sexual attraction before. And for that, I commend the author.<br /><br />Thorn, who one might see as the “romantic interest,” was the most unappealing “hero” I’ve ever met. He’s rude, secretive and treats Ophelia like a speck of dirt. Throughout the course of the book, the two never really warm up to each other, and I was frustrated by their “relationship.”<br /><br /><strong>3. Lots of troublesome content, especially for a "kids" book, including implied rape, physical and mental abuse, forced marriage and torture.</strong> Now, I’ve read a lot of books, and a lot of what I read is on the darker side, so abuse and rape are nothing new to me when it comes to fiction. But one character in particular was so loathsome and dangerous, he confesses to Ophelia (and at this point he doesn’t know who she is) that he can hardly wait to “deflower Thorn’s betrothed.” Keep in mind that this entire time I am picturing Ophelia as a twelve-year-old, because that’s how she acted. (She is, in fact, seventeen or eighteen, but I just couldn't picture her that age.)<br /><br />One of Ophelia’s uncles has some <i>
  great 
</i>advice for her, after she confesses that she has no intention of having sex with Thorn:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <p>
    “No, dear girl, no, forget that. Look at yourself. You’re the height of a stool and the weight of a bolster...However he makes you feel, I advise you never to set your will against that of your husband. You’ll end up with broken bones.”
    <br />
  </p>
</blockquote><br /><br />"Never set your will against that of your husband" is code for "let him do whatever the fuck he wants." I mean, this whole story feels very old-fashioned and I supposed that <em>used</em> to be the advice given to young women who are about to be married, but jeez!<br /><br /><strong>4. The world-building is full of great ideas, but it’s sort of all over the place.</strong> There are airships, floating islands, and each ark has a different magical ability. Ophelia can not only sense the history of an object when she touches it, but she can travel through mirrors. When she lands at the Pole, a sled with flying dogs takes them to the top of the city. In short, there is a lot of cool stuff packed into this story, but it never really felt cohesive, as if the author were simply throwing all her good ideas into the pot.<br /><br /><strong>5. The story grabbed me for about the first fifty pages or so, but once Ophelia reaches the Pole, the pacing slowed down tremendously.</strong> I really struggled to keep going, for some reason. And the fact that I didn’t like any of the characters made it doubly hard to finish.<br /><br />And the one character I did like? It was Ophelia’s scarf. Yes, you read that right. I loved her scarf, which is alive and has a mind of it’s own. I wanted to read <i>
  that 
</i>story, about Ophelia and her scarf!<br /><br />At the end of the day, this book just wasn’t for me. The constant barrage of physical and mental abuse thrown at Ophelia made me so sad and uncomfortable, and I ended up hating her because she never did anything about it! You’ll see plenty of five-star reviews on Goodreads (and oddly, most of them are written in French, so I’m not sure what that means…), so clearly there is an audience for this book. I’m sure Ophelia has many more adventures in store for her, but unfortunately, I won’t be there to see them.<a href="http://booksbonesbuffy.com/2018/10/08/a-winters-promise-by-christelle-dabos-review/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review originally appeared on Books, Bones &amp; Buffy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5069279886357667243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye*" href="/user/show/11652288-faye">Faye*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer18224056701328016297">I listened to this on audio so maybe I was just distracted but what the hell was this even about??? <br/><br/>The plot was so flimsy, I feel like nothing happened in the entire book. The world seemed so promising but also was sort of all over the place and Dabos did not give me enough information for me to be drawn into it. <br/><br/>The characters are alright but nothing to write home about, either. Ophelia, our MC, is the most timid and underwhelming main character I probably ever read about. She can “read” objec</span>
  <span id="freeText18224056701328016297" style="display:none">I listened to this on audio so maybe I was just distracted but what the hell was this even about??? <br /><br />The plot was so flimsy, I feel like nothing happened in the entire book. The world seemed so promising but also was sort of all over the place and Dabos did not give me enough information for me to be drawn into it. <br /><br />The characters are alright but nothing to write home about, either. Ophelia, our MC, is the most timid and underwhelming main character I probably ever read about. She can “read” objects with her hands and travel through mirrors but still manages to be more passive than a handkerchief. Which, by the way, she needs all the time because she is constantly sniffling and sneezing. To be fair, it is cold at the Pole and she is wearing damp clothes most of the book but PLEASE. Do we really need to read about it constantly? Basically, Ophelia reads as if she’s about twelve.<br /><br />For the rest of the characters, they didn’t interest me much either. The love interest Thorn’s only two distinguishing characteristics seem to be his brusqueness and his excessive height. <br /><br />As for the other characters and the rest of the “plot”, I would like to quote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/37149293-helena" rel="nofollow noopener">Helena</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2722361679?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a>, which I think sums it up perfectly: <br />“The whole Pole ark reminds me of a very bad telenovela. Is anyone sane? Is anyone not overly dramatic? Is anyone a decent person? Find out in the next episode of "Pole's court".”<br /><br />And finally, the tone in this book was just off somehow. I read like it was written for a young audience but the themes were too mature for children... <br /><br /><br />This sounds like I hated it, which isn't the case at all! In the end, I’m still rating this 3 stars because I had a good time listening but I just have to say it just felt like nothing happened in those 500+ pages and I have only a vague idea about what the story is about.</span>

<div id="review_2722361679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2722361679" />
    <a title="Helena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37149293-helena"><img alt="Helena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603672381p2/37149293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2722361679?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena" href="/user/show/37149293-helena">Helena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40969531-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37149293-helena?shelf=series-i-won-t-continue">series-i-won-t-continue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37149293-helena?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2722361679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11840534131924453001">2.5<br/>Imagine being tied up and having the best cake ever sitting in front of you but only being fed a spoonful once in a few hours. That's EXACTLY what it felt like reading this book. <br/><br/>Let's start on the positive note:<br/>-I loved the idea of the magic system, I loved the differences between the arks and the fact that most of it was kind of misterious so that we had to pay attention in order to understand them<br/>-Ophelia's great-uncle and her brother Hector were such nice characters, it made me so sad whe</span>
  <span id="freeText11840534131924453001" style="display:none">2.5<br />Imagine being tied up and having the best cake ever sitting in front of you but only being fed a spoonful once in a few hours. That's EXACTLY what it felt like reading this book. <br /><br />Let's start on the positive note:<br />-I loved the idea of the magic system, I loved the differences between the arks and the fact that most of it was kind of misterious so that we had to pay attention in order to understand them<br />-Ophelia's great-uncle and her brother Hector were such nice characters, it made me so sad when she had to leave without saying goodbye to them<br />-Descriptions, even though sometimes excesive, were nice and easy to imagine<br />And that would be it. In 500 pages, these are the only redeeming qualities I could think of.<br /><br />Now, since this is a fairly long book and almost nothing happens, it'd be easy to point out all the flaws but ain't nobody got the time. So here are a few I found most annoying:<br />-The story is stretched thin. By 60ish% mark NOTHING was happening. I don't mind a slow paced book but this doesn't have enough content to be one, we could've been introduced to so much more which could potentially improve the impression<br />-Ophelia. I honestly don't know if I like her or absolutely despise her. She seems more like a caricature than an actual character. It looks like the author tried too hard not to make her the "perfect female protagonist" to the point that everything seemed like an exaggeration. She's strong and smart at the beginning but twenty pages later, she's totally submissive to the will of her future husband and, not only that, she also apperantly forgets how to use a brain. And at the end, all of a sudden, she remembers who she was and is a badass again. Why?<br />-Random plot twists at most random times. Honestly, most of them made no sense. At some point I just learned to accept them for whatever reason and continue on but that doesn't mean I wasn't pissed because some of them.<br />-The whole Pole ark reminds me of a very bad telenovela. Is anyone sane? Is anyone not overly dramatic? Is anyone a decent person? Find out in the next episode of "Pole's court".<br /><br />I really hoped this would be a book for me, especially because I loved the magic part. I might try to pick up the second book once it's translated but my expectations aren't very high.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11840534131924453001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2514871589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2514871589" />
    <a title="rain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68699718-rain"><img alt="rain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602754816p2/68699718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2514871589?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rain" href="/user/show/68699718-rain">rain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/40969531-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2514871589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5546706856683864871">Thank you to Edelweiss for giving me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br/><br/>This book was my first approval on Edelweiss which is why it has a special spot in my heart. I actually have a huge ARC TBR pile (which I mainly got from netgalley) and it pains me sometimes when I start reading an ARC and it doesn't hold my attention and I just have to force myself to read it. THAT'S ACTUALLY ONE OF THE WORST BOOKDRAGON FEELINGS EVER. I feel bad when I DNF a book but I can't help it somet</span>
  <span id="freeText5546706856683864871" style="display:none">Thank you to Edelweiss for giving me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br />This book was my first approval on Edelweiss which is why it has a special spot in my heart. I actually have a huge ARC TBR pile (which I mainly got from netgalley) and it pains me sometimes when I start reading an ARC and it doesn't hold my attention and I just have to force myself to read it. THAT'S ACTUALLY ONE OF THE WORST BOOKDRAGON FEELINGS EVER. I feel bad when I DNF a book but I can't help it sometimes. <br /><br />I was scared to have the same experience in reading this book but my worries were for naught because THIS BOOK IS TOTALLY WORTH THE READ. My heart is overflowing with love for it. <br /><br />A Winter's Promise is a #1 French Bestseller and was originally published in 2013. Now, it has finally been translated to English by Hildegarde Serle and will be released on September 25! <br /><br />• I'm 100% pleased with the world-building<br />If a book has a detailed and well-written world, expect me to shriek about it for 1000 years. Which is exactly why I'm about to dedicate my life to shrieking about A Winter's Promise. <br /><br />This book is set at a time where the world has been divided into Arks which are starkly different from each other. I love how Christelle Dabos wrote Pole and Anima. These two Arks that were focused on the books were interesting and magical in the best possible ways. <br /><br />I am especially pleased with the dynamics of the Pole. It is made up of political intrigue, social hierarchy, warring clans, social scandals, and illusions which made it even more intriguing. <br /><br />Y'ALL NEED TO READ THIS BOOK SO WE CAN SHRIEK ABOUT IT TOGETHER.<br /><br />• ‎I fell in love with the magic system<br /><br />This book features a magic system where a person inherits the magic of the family. There are families of illusionists, animists, and those who can inflict pain on others (Painists??? Maybe not). Anyway, it was fascinating to learn the different abilities of the different clans and uncover the intrigue surrounding them. In this book, you don't know who to trust. Everyone has secrets and hidden motives and I just love books that fry my last three brain cells. Some books are unforgiving like that. Poor brain cells. <br /><br />• ‎Three-dimensional characters!!!<br /><br />All the characters here are well-written. Most of them have complex personalities and I can't wait to learn more about them in the sequel. <br /><br />— Ophelia is the protagonist and my new fave. I just relate so much to this girl I felt like I was reading about myself. She loves reading, she's an expert at breaking dishes, she has a strong will and most of all, SHE DOESN'T HAVE A SENSE OF DIRECTION. That's me right there. I don't even know what my life would be when I move to a city for college. I think I will get lost in the darkest recesses of Underworld in 3 nanoseconds. Send help. <br /><br />I also love Ophelia's I-don't-need-a-man-to-make-myself-complete attitude. But I also ship her and Thorn so much everything hurts. Why do I love slow burn relationships that are even more complicated than my physics lessons???<br /><br />—Thorn is the male protagonist and I JUST WANT TO PROTECT HIM WITH MY LIFE. I think a block of stone shows more emotions than him but for some reasons unknown, I have come to love this character so much. Beneath his hard exterior and cold expressions is a soft heart. At least I hope so. I can't wait to see where his relationship with Ophelia goes in the next book. GIVE ME THE SEQUEL NOW PLEASE. <br /><br />—Berenilde is Thorn's aunt and I don't know if I want to trust her or throw her from a 720-story building. Based from my mixed emotions, I can say that she's a complex character with an interesting personality.<br /><br />—Rosaline is Ophelia's godmother and the only member of her chaotic family to accompany her to the Pole. I adore how she's so strict to Ophelia but will also protect her with her own life. <br /><br />—Archibald is a character I want to read more about. I have a feeling that he will have a huge role in the next books. He's one of the most interesting characters in this book and if he isn't given more attention in the sequel, I'll wage a war on the lizards in my house out of anger. <br /><br />—Kudos to Ophelia's loyal scarf who adores her and will probably strangle her one of these days if it gets upset. <br /><br />There are a lot more characters you need to know about and I would appreciate it if you pick up this book so we can talk about them and decide which characters to throw out of a 720-story building. <br /><br />• ‎Has an atmospheric vibe<br />This is the first translated book I have ever read and I'm pleased that my first experience was positive. I don't know if the original exudes the same feels but this version has an atmospheric tone which I absolutely loved. This book totally transported me to a different world and I forgot about the quizzes I needed to study for, the homeworks I needed to answer, the researches I needed to write, and the reports I needed to make just for a little while. It gave me the perfect break from reality and I'm so thanful for that. <br /><br />• ‎Story is well-established AND I WANT MORE<br />Since this is just the first book to the series, it's mainly just the establishment of the characters, the world, and the plot. I enjoyed every page of it and now I'm chewing the nearest table with impatience BECAUSE I NEED TO READ THE SEQUEL ASAP. I want more of the characters and this world. I want to know how the bigger picture will unfold. I don't know when I'll be able to read the next book or find a copy but I'm really hoping I can read it because I'll be destroyed if I can't. <br /><br />A Winter's Promise offered me a place of refuge when I needed it most. It's a highly unique story full of mysteries and intrigue and I 20/10 recommend it to all bookdragons who love fantasy and awesomeness. <br /><br />This book will be published on September 25 and I really hope that more people will pick it up so they can be swept away by the world Christelle Dabos has created.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5546706856683864871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2695998764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2695998764" />
    <a title="Mary-ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8288505-mary-ellen"><img alt="Mary-ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377600080p2/8288505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2695998764?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary-ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary-ellen" href="/user/show/8288505-mary-ellen">Mary-ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925603828" href="/book/show/40723006-a-winter-s-promise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2695998764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16943405362950571575">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this YA fantasy by Christelle Dabos. The English language version of the first book in the series only became available late last year. I picked it up because I liked the cover and it sounded interesting. I’m so glad I did.<br/><br/>The world-building is fabulous. The world has been smashed to pieces and now consists of a number of floating Arks. Each Ark seems to specialise in it’s own style of magic. Ophelia comes from Anima. She has the ability to read objects, understand</span>
  <span id="freeText16943405362950571575" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this YA fantasy by Christelle Dabos. The English language version of the first book in the series only became available late last year. I picked it up because I liked the cover and it sounded interesting. I’m so glad I did.<br /><br />The world-building is fabulous. The world has been smashed to pieces and now consists of a number of floating Arks. Each Ark seems to specialise in it’s own style of magic. Ophelia comes from Anima. She has the ability to read objects, understanding the history of the object and the emotions of those who have come into contact with it. She can also walk through mirrors in different locations. <br /><br />Having dodged two previous engagements, there is no escape for Ophelia when a marriage is arranged between her and Thorn. Her austere fiancé quickly whisks her away to her new home, the distant Ark of the Pole. Here she is thrown into a world of court intrigue, dynastic politics and constant danger. When Ophelia begins to unravel the many layers of secrets in her new world, and comes to understand what is expected of her, she is not happy with what she discovers.<br /><br />There is a quiet strength to Ophelia’s character that makes her immensely likeable. Despite the severity of his character, I also like Thorn. I’m looking forward to seeing how things play out between them. The story moves at a good pace, and the language is often rich and atmospheric, especially the early chapters. When I started to read this story, I instantly felt I had a book of quality in my hands. Hildegarde Serle clearly did a nice job on the translation.<br /><br />The book ends with Ophelia about to be thrust into a situation where she must face significant new challenges and dangers, and I can’t wait for book 2 to become available in English. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16943405362950571575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eH2JmHO+6f6vzYSYS0w8dzNMbCNrW6y7J7ZxZe9i6L3iuzIAobXVt6wudUpouLa+kffQ8wBpqN1Tw//i3hMs9Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2ILvVtQ/xEOQyBTRWUWCLi8v5wLmc7HsJEuPENdQVeZCRFTOBjT4CpMr5QN6sQjnjZRb0o1BtYpQPgGX5iGRrg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7123624.Christelle_Dabos">About Christelle Dabos</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7123624.Christelle_Dabos"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1592900793p3/7123624.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11138087846562985411">Christelle Dabos est née en 1980 sur la Côte d’Azur et a grandi dans un foyer empli de musique classique et d’énigmes historiques. Plus imaginative que cérébrale, elle commence à gribouiller ses premiers textes sur les bancs de la faculté. Installée en Belgique, elle se destine à être bibliothécaire quand la maladie survient. L’écriture devient alors une évasion hors de la machinerie médicale, pui</span>
  <span id="freeText11138087846562985411" style="display:none">Christelle Dabos est née en 1980 sur la Côte d’Azur et a grandi dans un foyer empli de musique classique et d’énigmes historiques. Plus imaginative que cérébrale, elle commence à gribouiller ses premiers textes sur les bancs de la faculté. Installée en Belgique, elle se destine à être bibliothécaire quand la maladie survient. L’écriture devient alors une évasion hors de la machinerie médicale, puis une lente reconstruction et enfin une seconde nature. Elle bénéficie pendant ce temps de l’émulation de Plume d’Argent, une communauté d’auteurs sur Internet. C’est grâce à leurs encouragements qu’elle décide de relever son tout premier défi littéraire : s’inscrire au Concours du Premier roman jeunesse. Grande lauréate parmi les trois finalistes, Christelle Dabos écrit actuellement le troisème livre de La Passe-miroir.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11138087846562985411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

            <nobr>
